    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer17152091779946173490">THE RIVETING SEQUEL TO THE HIT BOOK <i>YOU</i>, NOW A NETFLIX SERIES<br/><br/>In the compulsively readable sequel to her widely acclaimed debut novel, You, Caroline Kepnes weaves a tale that <i>Booklist</i> calls “the love child of Holden Caulfield and Patrick Bateman.”<br/><br/>Joe Goldberg is no stranger to hiding bodies.   <span id="freeText17152091779946173490" style="display:none">THE RIVETING SEQUEL TO THE HIT BOOK <i>YOU</i>, NOW A NETFLIX SERIES<br /><br />In the compulsively readable sequel to her widely acclaimed debut novel, You, Caroline Kepnes weaves a tale that <i>Booklist</i> calls “the love child of Holden Caulfield and Patrick Bateman.”<br /><br />Joe Goldberg is no stranger to hiding bodies. In the past ten years, this thirty-something has buried four of them, collateral damage in his quest for love. Now he’s heading west to Los Angeles, the city of second chances, determined to put his past behind him.<br /><br />In Hollywood, Joe blends in effortlessly with the other young upstarts. He eats guac, works in a bookstore, and flirts with a journalist neighbor. But while others seem fixated on their own reflections, Joe can’t stop looking over his shoulder. The problem with hidden bodies is that they don’t always stay that way. They re-emerge, like dark thoughts, multiplying and threatening to destroy what Joe wants most: true love. And when he finds it in a darkened room in Soho House, he’s more desperate than ever to keep his secrets buried. He doesn’t want to hurt his new girlfriend—he wants to be with her forever. But if she ever finds out what he’s done, he may not have a choice…</span>
  <a data-text-id="17152091779946173490" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1499929365" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1499929365" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1499929365?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/23492288-hidden-bodies">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1499929365" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9590423519360125683"><blockquote>
  <i>I buy violets for Amy. Not roses. Roses are for people who did something wrong. I have done everything right this time around. I’m a good boyfriend. I chose well.</i>
</blockquote><br/>And so begins the sequel to Kepnes' beautiful little mindfuck - <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20821614.You__You___1_' title='You (You, #1) by Caroline Kepnes' rel='nofollow noopener'>You</a>. We are taken, once again, inside the mind of Joe Goldberg as he, yet again, pursues his "true love". This time, his adventures take him all the way to Los Angeles.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23492288.Hidden_Bodies__You___2_' title='Hidden Bodies (You, #2) by Caroline Kepnes' rel='nofollow noopener'>Hidden Bodies</a> is good, but honestly, Kepnes has lost a little magic here. I think it was always going </span>
  <span id="freeText9590423519360125683" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>I buy violets for Amy. Not roses. Roses are for people who did something wrong. I have done everything right this time around. I’m a good boyfriend. I chose well.</i>
</blockquote><br />And so begins the sequel to Kepnes' beautiful little mindfuck - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20821614.You__You___1_" title="You (You, #1) by Caroline Kepnes" rel="nofollow noopener">You</a>. We are taken, once again, inside the mind of Joe Goldberg as he, yet again, pursues his "true love". This time, his adventures take him all the way to Los Angeles.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23492288.Hidden_Bodies__You___2_" title="Hidden Bodies (You, #2) by Caroline Kepnes" rel="nofollow noopener">Hidden Bodies</a> is good, but honestly, Kepnes has lost a little magic here. I think it was always going to be hard. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20821614.You__You___1_" title="You (You, #1) by Caroline Kepnes" rel="nofollow noopener">You</a> presented us with a unique kind of narrator - the kind of charming, intelligent, witty sociopath that we all loved to hate. Armed with gorgeous prose and an underlying murderous quality, Joe was something new and surprising.<br /><br />This book is... <b>more of the same</b>. It's beautifully-written and the writing has a dynamic flow that keeps the pages moving quickly, and yet there's no spark of discovery. Readers will come to this book knowing what to expect from Joe and getting it, which, while sometimes enjoyable, does not add much to the story.<br /><br />Joe's narrative is as dark and hilarious as before. I especially liked his criticisms of Los Angeles; even though I personally love the city, it's funny to see his perspective as a New Yorker. His observations are witty and oh so true.<br /><br />But, where the first book was different and shocking, this book was merely "fun". I personally feel <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20821614.You__You___1_" title="You (You, #1) by Caroline Kepnes" rel="nofollow noopener">You</a> ended in a perfect place to haunt its readers and make them think long after they put the book down. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23492288.Hidden_Bodies__You___2_" title="Hidden Bodies (You, #2) by Caroline Kepnes" rel="nofollow noopener">Hidden Bodies</a> attempts to add to a story that didn't really need to be extended - and it shows. <br /><br />The plot occasionally felt like rambling. Joe was less exciting to read about. So, while an entertaining commentary, this book just wasn't needed.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://society6.com/bookgeek/" rel="nofollow noopener">Store</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9590423519360125683" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2695853801" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2695853801" />
    <a title="Emma Giordano" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano"><img alt="Emma Giordano" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569693958p2/30604861.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2695853801?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Giordano" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Giordano" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano">Emma Giordano</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/23492288-hidden-bodies">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30604861-emma-giordano?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2695853801" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12202718487087704424">I’m sorry, but this book was not good at all. A super unnecessary sequel that lost absolutely everything that made <i>You</i> such a hit. I don’t think it’s possible for me to be more disappointed. This is one of my least favorite books I’ve ever read.<br/> <br/>CW: stalking, violence, murder, substance abuse<br/><br/>I was deeply disappointed with the direction of Joe’s character. In <i>You</i>, Joe has a unique path of development. It’s clear he is a very twisted man who does horrible, irredeemable things, yet there are moment</span>
  <span id="freeText12202718487087704424" style="display:none">I’m sorry, but this book was not good at all. A super unnecessary sequel that lost absolutely everything that made <i>You</i> such a hit. I don’t think it’s possible for me to be more disappointed. This is one of my least favorite books I’ve ever read.<br /> <br />CW: stalking, violence, murder, substance abuse<br /><br />I was deeply disappointed with the direction of Joe’s character. In <i>You</i>, Joe has a unique path of development. It’s clear he is a very twisted man who does horrible, irredeemable things, yet there are moments that make him seem a <i>little</i> less terrible which keep you fascinated enough to keep reading. The only words I could use to describe Joe in <i>Hidden Bodies</i> is straight up homicidal. In <i>You</i>, he has reasons behind his violent acts - albeit, deluded reasons - but he leads the reader to believe he’s acting out of his own perverse conscience. In <i>Hidden Bodies</i>, if a character breathes wrong, he goes off on a tangent about all the different ways he’d like to murder them. I get that a large part of <i>You</i> is following Joe as he gets more involved with stalking Beck and takes increasing risks to achieve his goals, but it’s as if we hit the height of his character at the end and there was nowhere else for him to go in the second installment. Additionally, his overall characterization was watered down. In book one, it was clear Joe genuinely believed he was in love with Beck and working towards her greater interests, but I refuse to believe Joe “loved” any of the women he claimed to love in book two. (I mean you can also argue Joe was never capable of loving Beck in the first place, but my point is in regard to how Joe treats the new love interests in comparison to Beck when he claims to love them even MORE than her.) There was no chemistry, nothing from Joe’s end to suggest he felt more than attracted towards them, yet the author attempts to fabricate this nonexistent emotion from Joe. Moreover, the secondary characters were so vapid and one-dimensional. The characters of <i>You</i> were all equally flawed and infuriating, but they <b>brought</b> something to the story. They were unique and necessary. Every character in <i>Hidden Bodies</i> could have been replaced with any stereotypical Los Angeles “wannabe” with interpersonal issues. There was nothing enticing about ANY character in this book, which made it much more difficult to sit through their flat personalities.<br /><br />Another shining element of <i>You</i> that is absent in <i>Hidden Bodies</i> was the second person narrative. Having a story told from the perspective of a stalker with a dual relationship TO the person being stalked without their knowledge was creepy, unsettling, and extremely unique. Without Joe telling the story to Beck, it lost all that magic that was created in book one. Obviously, the perspective had to change but in doing so, it reverted the book to any other adult thriller. The writing itself was fair; I can’t say I noticed a significant decline from <i>You</i>, but it was no longer notable.<br /><br />The plot was also SUPER boring. I could not stand to put down <i>You</i> but I was begging for the end of <i>Hidden Bodies</i> very early on. Even the moments that should have evoked suspense and intensity were muted due to the lack of chemistry between characters and lack of urgency because everyone else was just SO DUMB. The worst part is that that the most exciting plot twist from <i>Hidden Bodies</i> was actually a twist that was reused from <i>You</i>. Even with all of the decline from book one, we couldn’t just get something new in a sequel to a best-selling novel? It almost felt like the author gave up trying to create something fresh within this world and tried to rely on the success of book one to sell the sequel. <br /><br />The SINGULAR decent part of <i>Hidden Bodies</i> is when the storyline does cross over back to the events of <i>You</i> (Despite being a sequel, the premise of book two doesn’t actually have much to do with the actual events of book one for a lot of the story). This was the only part of the novel to make me excited to find out what happened next and captured what I loved about book one. Then again, it just further proves that <i>Hidden Bodies</i> is woefully subpar to it’s predecessor and it was nowhere near enough to carry this story.<br /><br />Overall, this book was a total disappointment. If you enjoyed <i>You</i> as much as myself, be kind to yourself and skip this one. This is the most unnecessary sequel to ever be written. I desperately wish I hadn’t read it and allowed it to partially taint my view of one of my favorite thriller novels. Not worth your time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12202718487087704424" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2717743318" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2717743318" />
    <a title="Maria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/77602709-maria"><img alt="Maria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1519184646p2/77602709.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2717743318?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria" href="/user/show/77602709-maria">Maria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781471192647" href="/book/show/50040404-hidden-bodies">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2717743318" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7294591076228310600"><b>1.3</b>/5 Stars ⭐️<br/><br/><blockquote>“It is possible to know people. They show you who they are. You just have to be looking.”</blockquote><br/><br/>Oh boy. Where do I begin? Have you ever felt like reading a book could manifest itself? Like you could actually have not only mental but physical symptoms from the experience? I felt like death was coming while reading it. <b>Coronavirus has nothing on this</b>. And I actually finished this book while on quarantine.<br/><br/>This book contains more Woody Allen references than Riverdale's random pop culture refe</span>
  <span id="freeText7294591076228310600" style="display:none"><b>1.3</b>/5 Stars ⭐️<br /><br /><blockquote>“It is possible to know people. They show you who they are. You just have to be looking.”</blockquote><br /><br />Oh boy. Where do I begin? Have you ever felt like reading a book could manifest itself? Like you could actually have not only mental but physical symptoms from the experience? I felt like death was coming while reading it. <b>Coronavirus has nothing on this</b>. And I actually finished this book while on quarantine.<br /><br />This book contains more Woody Allen references than Riverdale's random pop culture references. <b>This book loves the smell of its own farts and cum</b>. This book is more pretentious than an actual Woody Allen movie and there's nothing more pretentious than that. I wanted to punch every single character more than I wanted to punch <i>Timothée Chalamet's little pretentious Woody Allen esque character in A Rainy Day in New York (2019)</i>. I HATE EVERYTHING.<br /><br />I can't believe how much this book deviates from its predecessor. Yes, YOU isn't a perfect book, it's very problematic actually but it's thrilling and it grips you tight in. This one... has nothing to hold your attention. This book is just <b>Joe spewing out hate towards L.A. pretentious people while HIMSELF spews out pretentious shit like a L.A. person while in L.A. himself</b>. Ah, yes. Exactly like a Woody Allen film. Ugh there are also so much Manson and Cosby mentions here, the only one missing was Weinstein honestly! Jeez.<br /><br />I had heard the worst motherfucking shit about this banger here. From Goodreads users, booktubers even a friend. Of course, I'm such a completist, I just had to see how the second season was in the book like. Don't get me wrong, the second season wasn't a marvel of television but it was intriguing. And then I find out of course... <b>THEY CHANGED LIKE 90% OF THE BOOK</b>. This is the only time I can condone this kind of action. I mostly want movies and tv shows to be exact copies of their source material, like all book lovers of course. <b>IF</b> the source material is of merit. <b>IF</b> the source material is straight out of the garbage, then YES NETFLIX DRAG 'EM.<br /><br />This book has Candace on the cover while Candace in the book world is DEAD. Why did they make a media tie in version of this with this particular Netflix poster? Couldn't they remove Candace? They might as well add Beck on the mix. I'm a graphic designer, I can fix that up for you fellas. So incompetent. I'm so tired of this bullshit.<br /><br /><b>Don't read this book, don't even think about reading this book</b>. If you want to indulge yourself with these characters and world, <b>watch the show</b>. The second season is like 90% different than this mess. <b>IF</b> you see me picking up the third and the fourth books (why is this a thing) slap me, kill me, bully me, idk what. I'm very OCD about not completing things but I can't do this to myself! Thank you and goodbye.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7294591076228310600" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1367767964" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1367767964" />
    <a title="Candace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16384209-candace"><img alt="Candace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459720769p2/16384209.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1367767964?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Candace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Candace" href="/user/show/16384209-candace">Candace</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/29348770-hidden-bodies">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=dangerous-hero-themed-books-read">dangerous-hero-themed-books-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=revenge-stories">revenge-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=listened-to-audio-version">listened-to-audio-version</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=hate-that-i-love-them">hate-that-i-love-them</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=pregnant-heroines">pregnant-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=wtf-did-i-just-read">wtf-did-i-just-read</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1367767964" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14121137782044251610">I loved 'You' and started 'Hidden Bodies' immediately after I finished it. Looking back, I think that maybe I should have taken a break from the endearingly crazy Joe. Two books full of his rants and rationalizations back to back was just too much. Joe's special brand of crazy is probably best served in small doses. I absolutely loved him, but soon grew irritated with his antics. You really can get too much of a good thing.<br/><br/>After the way things ended for Beck, Joe finds a new object of obsession,</span>
  <span id="freeText14121137782044251610" style="display:none">I loved 'You' and started 'Hidden Bodies' immediately after I finished it. Looking back, I think that maybe I should have taken a break from the endearingly crazy Joe. Two books full of his rants and rationalizations back to back was just too much. Joe's special brand of crazy is probably best served in small doses. I absolutely loved him, but soon grew irritated with his antics. You really can get too much of a good thing.<br /><br />After the way things ended for Beck, Joe finds a new object of obsession, Amy. Pretty soon, he's following her - unbeknownst to her, of course - across the country. In no time, Joe integrates himself into the lifestyle of a struggling Hollywood writer. <br /><br />Along the way, Joe makes some new friends and gains some new love interests. As we know, where there is a love interest for Joe, there's bound to be some hidden bodies. This book was no exception.<br /><br />Overall, I found this to be a good story. I think I would have liked it more if I had taken a little break between books 1 and 2. I absolutely love Joe as a character, but by midway through 'Hidden Bodies' his craziness was starting to get on my nerves. I think his quirks are best handled a little at a time. I give it 3.5 stars.<br /><br />See more of my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.bookaddicthaven.com">www.bookaddicthaven.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14121137782044251610" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText4893468255177827694" style="display:none">DNF at page 84<br /><br />I wasn't kidding when I said this is the worst book I've ever read. This is seriously the worst book I've ever read. Every other book I actually finished and awarded one star and every other book I never finished because it sucked... all of those books are a million times better than this garbage that masquerades itself as a book. <br /><br />Caroline Kepnes has to be a pseudonym for a thirteen year old boy who just learned about sex from his friend and spends his days watching porn and eating Cheetos. This is the most poorly written excuse for a book ever, and Kepnes can't put a sentence together without something explicit, sexual or otherwise. There are so many more deserving authors who could benefit from a glimmer of the spotlight she has somehow drunkenly staggered herself into these days. <br /><br />There is not one redeeming quality about this book. It's pretentious, disgusting, uninspired, juvenile, immature, pathetic, and sad. It deserves no place in any bookstore or library, and all copies of this book should be burned or buried somewhere so we can all forget it was ever written.</span>

<div id="review_1447200119" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1447200119" />
    <a title="Esil" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3643764-esil"><img alt="Esil" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1443746908p2/3643764.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1447200119?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Esil" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Esil" href="/user/show/3643764-esil">Esil</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/23492288-hidden-bodies">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3643764-esil?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1447200119" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer426391807350208503">Oh dear, Ms. Kepnes. You got me with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20821614.You__You___1_' title='You (You, #1) by Caroline Kepnes' rel='nofollow noopener'>You</a>, but clearly you were out to get someone else with Hidden Bodies. What I found clever and enticing in You seems to have vanished, and in its place you took me on a crude meandering journey that felt too long -- way too long -- and pointless. In fact, it’s almost like you knew exactly what to do to shake me off. Instead of the bookish New York setting in You, you set Hidden Bodies in Hollywood with no literary references whatsoever. And focusing on Hollywo</span>
  <span id="freeText426391807350208503" style="display:none">Oh dear, Ms. Kepnes. You got me with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20821614.You__You___1_" title="You (You, #1) by Caroline Kepnes" rel="nofollow noopener">You</a>, but clearly you were out to get someone else with Hidden Bodies. What I found clever and enticing in You seems to have vanished, and in its place you took me on a crude meandering journey that felt too long -- way too long -- and pointless. In fact, it’s almost like you knew exactly what to do to shake me off. Instead of the bookish New York setting in You, you set Hidden Bodies in Hollywood with no literary references whatsoever. And focusing on Hollywood, you mocked the vapid world of the wannabe young actors and film makers -- but that got old – and did I mention crude -- pretty quickly. And you even dropped the second person singular narrative voice that had really got me in You. And Joe the stalker just seemed icky and pathetic – there was nothing tugging at my sympathy strings this time. I almost gave up a few times -- and I must confess that I did some pretty heavy duty skimming -- but I had to read to the end to make sure you hadn’t set some kind of trap for me somewhere along the way. But no – from beginning to end, you were determined to shake me off. Hey, I get it, you’ve moved on and now you clearly have your sights on someone else. And it looks like you’ve succeeded, because many readers seem to have loved Hidden Bodies. That’s fine. My feelings aren’t hurt. You’ve lost interest in me. I’ve lost interest in you. Thank you to Netgalley and the publisher for an opportunity to read an advance copy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="426391807350208503" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

While <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1097376146?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">You </a> was written all about the “you” Joe happened to be <s>stalking</s> enamored with, <i>Hidden Bodies</i> is all about the “we” as Joe finds love. <br><br>This is one of those series (and Joe is one of those characters) that you either get or you don’t. <div id="review_2016789017" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2016789017" />
    <a title="James" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7365405-james"><img alt="James" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1522094190p2/7365405.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2016789017?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James" href="/user/show/7365405-james">James</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/23492288-hidden-bodies">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7365405-james?shelf=3-multi-book-series">3-multi-book-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7365405-james?shelf=9-read-2017-07-july">9-read-2017-07-july</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7365405-james?shelf=1-fiction">1-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2016789017" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1324110084688539764">3 out of 5 stars to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23492288.Hidden_Bodies__You___2_' title='Hidden Bodies (You, #2) by Caroline Kepnes' rel='nofollow noopener'>Hidden Bodies</a>, the second book in a thriller and suspense series by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/202260.Caroline_Kepnes' title='Caroline Kepnes' rel='nofollow noopener'>Caroline Kepnes</a>. Last month, my buddy Medhat suggested a read of You, the first novel in the series. It was such a fantastic book, probably in my top 2 of 2017 to date, that I had to continue reading the series. I've heard rumors there will be a third book, but I've yet to see it confirmed. I need to check on that! I am also completely excited as Lifetime is turning the books into a television series. I can't</span>
  <span id="freeText1324110084688539764" style="display:none">3 out of 5 stars to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23492288.Hidden_Bodies__You___2_" title="Hidden Bodies (You, #2) by Caroline Kepnes" rel="nofollow noopener">Hidden Bodies</a>, the second book in a thriller and suspense series by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/202260.Caroline_Kepnes" title="Caroline Kepnes" rel="nofollow noopener">Caroline Kepnes</a>. Last month, my buddy Medhat suggested a read of You, the first novel in the series. It was such a fantastic book, probably in my top 2 of 2017 to date, that I had to continue reading the series. I've heard rumors there will be a third book, but I've yet to see it confirmed. I need to check on that! I am also completely excited as Lifetime is turning the books into a television series. I can't wait... but until then, let's get on with the review of this second book. While I enjoyed several parts of it, it doesn't hold a candle to the first book and I'll explain why below.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <u>Plot, Characters &amp; Setting</u>
  </i>
</b><br />When we left off at the end of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20821614.You__You___1_" title="You (You, #1) by Caroline Kepnes" rel="nofollow noopener">You</a>, our protagonist/villain, Joe, completed his vicious cycle of crossing many lines and breaking tons of laws in NYC all in the name of love, also known to most people as stalking your prey. Yet he escaped without anyone knowing of his crimes and found himself falling in love with a new potential victim, Amy Adam. Joe begins trusting Amy, realizing she's a much-improved version of his last girlfriend, Beck. Amy begins pushing him for a key to his bookstore, which we all know from reading the first book contains a few secrets Joe would prefer stay buried, like some bodies. He hides everything as much as he possibly can, caving in to his girlfriend in order to hold on to her. When he arrives for work a few days later, the place has been robbed and Amy is missing. Did she do it? Was she kidnapped as payback for his prior crimes? What does she know? You'll find out... he finds a lead that shows she may be in Los Angeles. Joe quits his job and moves cross-country, where he meets an interesting cast of characters in his typical LA apartment. He negotiates/manipulates his way into working closely with a few Hollywood type agents and producers, finding himself falling in love with a new woman, coincidentally named Love.<br /><br />Love is perfect for Joe. She adores him. And he soon forgets about Amy. All seems well for a short period of time. But he keeps worrying about the one piece of evidence of his former crimes back in Rhode Island... and it drives him nearly insane, especially when the case is re-opened. He knows he has to find a way to retrieve it without anyone seeing him in the victim's house. Unfortunately, he's distracted by Delilah, one of the women in his apartment complex who has the hots for him. And then there's a cop who has taken a dislike to Joe, tailing him at different parts of the day while Joe is trying to tie up loose ends. But it's when Love's ex-boyfriend and her brother monopolize all of Love's time, Joe goes off the rails. As he begins to unwind, adding more and more crimes to his list in order to cover up the past and protect himself from losing Love, Joe finds himself getting careless. It all comes crashing down in the last few chapters of the book, ending at a place where it's very clear, a third book is necessary. Readers will not be OK with this ending, as it opens more holes than the one's Joe's already had to dig for each of his hidden bodies.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <u>Approach &amp; Style</u>
  </i>
</b><br />Whereas in the first book, Joe talks to the readers almost as if they are Beck, it's quite different in this second book. It's still told in first person with the perspective only on Joe throughout the whole story; however, there's no concept of "you" this time around. It works just as well, given the title is no longer "You," which means alternative progression is an expected path.<br /><br />I read a large-sized soft-cover book with ~430 pages. There are 56 chapters, so each one is less than 8 pages long on average. It took me 4 days over the course of a week, as I couldn't read each day; in total, probably about 6 hours. Some sections are a bit slow-paced while others are ultimate page-turners where you probably skip every fifth word just to see more quickly what's happening.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <u>Strengths</u>
  </i>
</b><br />Kepnes can certainly dream up extremely aggravating and realistic characters. Everyone she incorporates feels like someone I've met before, and at times, I wish I could be Joe and punish them for the things they say and do. But I'm a good guy and I don't commit many crimes. I mean any crimes.<br /><br />When she's on point with a dramatic scene, the plot and action is amazing. A few scenes were just as good as the initial book, especially when Joe is dealing with Delilah and the cop. It's almost like we never left the first book. <br /><br />Love is a really multi-dimensional woman; she has moments of brilliance followed by sheer silliness. I want her to be with Joe, but sometimes, she seems too good for him.<br /><br />The settings are crystal clear for the most part. I can always tell where we are and whether it's gonna be a safe zone or all hands to the battle field.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <u>Concerns</u>
  </i>
</b><br />It was such a let-down from the first book. Joe became weak. I didn't buy his drama. He seemed to cause problems for the sake of causing problems. He had the girl. But he let himself get caught up in other areas, ones that made him a true criminal and not a man in love. That's where he becomes a bad stalker. In the first book, he loved the girl so much, you could see why he did the things he did. This time, I struggled connecting with his motivation. He became every other evil antagonist, rather than the guy you wanted to root for.<br /><br />The ending gets closer to the original strength, but not all the way. I was pleasantly surprised when the last 100 or so pages took the story in quite a different and unexpected direction, but it wasn't enough to turn the book around for me. If this were the only book I read, and I didn't know much about the original plot, it wouldn't have been a book I'd recommend to friends. And that's sad because Joe is an amazing villain. I toyed with giving this less than 3 stars but I know that is mostly the disappointment in ruining a good character. It's redeemable in a third book, so I will have faith things get better.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <u>Final Thoughts</u>
  </i>
</b><br />The story is still good. It's got major problems with his constant quest for sex, which is just an overused plot component in this book. Pull that out. Take out the section where he turns into a whiny mess. And maybe give him a few more close calls, and we're back in the game.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <u>About Me</u>
  </i>
</b><br />For those new to me or my reviews... here's the scoop: I read A LOT. I write A LOT. And now I blog A LOT. First the book review goes on Goodreads, and then I send it on over to my WordPress blog at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://thisismytruthnow.com">https://thisismytruthnow.com</a>, where you'll also find TV &amp; Film reviews, the revealing and introspective 365 Daily Challenge and lots of blogging about places I've visited all over the world. And you can find all my social media profiles to get the details on the who/what/when/where and my pictures. Leave a comment and let me know what you think. Vote in the poll and ratings. Thanks for stopping by. <i>Note</i>: All written content is my original creation and copyrighted to me, but the graphics and images were linked from other sites and belong to them. Many thanks to their original creators.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15856993492786153211">I always worry when a second book in a series comes out- will it be a good as the first one? In this case...I would have to say a BIG YES! If you loved Joe as much as I did in- <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/956632218?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>You</a>...You will not mind having him weed out some of the pesky folk that have the unfortunate fate- to come up against him in the sequel- HIDDEN BODIES.<br/><br/>...and do I feel guilty for loving a serial killer that sees some of these idiots as mere inconveniences to be be brushed aside to make his life easier? No...no I don't. Af</span>
  <span id="freeText15856993492786153211" style="display:none">I always worry when a second book in a series comes out- will it be a good as the first one? In this case...I would have to say a BIG YES! If you loved Joe as much as I did in- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/956632218?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">You</a>...You will not mind having him weed out some of the pesky folk that have the unfortunate fate- to come up against him in the sequel- HIDDEN BODIES.<br><br>...and do I feel guilty for loving a serial killer that sees some of these idiots as mere inconveniences to be be brushed aside to make his life easier? No...no I don't. After all this is fiction...and they are reeaaaaaaaaaaaally annoying. Go Joe! ;)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456105522i/18190229.jpg" alt=" photo 6d1f5044-68b2-48e0-96c6-028044dcba2c_zpsusxm5srs.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Joe is back! And after his relationship with Beck "ended" in YOU- Joe quickly sets his sights on the mysterious Amy. She shows up looking for employment at the perfect time and Joe is intrigued. Where Beck was an open book, laying everything out online for him to track and follow, Amy believes in none of that. He hires her...and shortly after, makes her his girlfriend- and falls head over heels.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456105522i/18190228.jpg" alt=" photo b01efda0-295b-483b-aff1-02c30e8eba21_zpsproerbrt.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>For awhile life is wonderful- and Joe settles into utter bliss with "off the grid" Amy...but as her true nature reveals itself- he realizes finding a girl exactly the opposite of Beck may not have been the wisest choice. Now that she has deceived him and fled- finding and dealing with her is a tad more complicated than he would have liked.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456105522i/18190230.jpg" alt=" photo 17163c41-2d42-4476-9f09-546926b7c52d_zpsnqawlerq.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So Joe packs his bags and leaves New York City, following Amy's almost non-existent trail to Los Angles...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456105522i/18190231.jpg" alt=" photo ded93e77-3084-4dcf-8706-b238b0cd8e84_zpsuyumkzsz.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>....entering a very different world than he was used to....and getting sidetracked from his mission to rid the world of Amy- when he meets THE REAL girl of his dreams...Love.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456105522i/18190232.jpg" alt=" photo 790d54f8-2479-47d3-9db7-3153952d9705_zpsfcu8o3nv.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>...but Love comes with her own set of problems. As Joe is finding out the hard way- no girl is perfect...sometimes unfortunately for him...and sometimes unfortunately for her. Which category Love fits in- You will have to read to find out.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456105522i/18190233.jpg" alt=" photo 5216ab15-ab4a-425a-9440-34b22da5c131_zpsx0lebyyh.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In the most simple terms- if you loved Joe the first time- you will probably love him the second time. If you hated him and found his journey to find a soulmate that he didn't want to kill less than satisfying- the odds are you should probably stop at YOU...but seriously what fun would that be?<br><br>Thank you NetGalley for providing me this gloooooooooooorious book to read and review!</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6603759-misericordia-the-serendipity-aegis?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2792790076" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14397243843169563569"><b>It all goes like that: </b> Q: Oh, fuck. Double thousand triple fuckity fuck. (c) <br/><br/>The 2nd book is even better than the 1st one, imho. The author is going to be very careful so that the3d one doesn't repeat Harris' flop with his 3d vol of Hannibal Lecter. Joe & Love are such precocious characters that I have no idea what path would let the 3d book to be at least equal in standing with its predecessors.<br/><br/>Q:<br/><b>I smile. We exist. We are both on a journey and we are both in love and that’s all anyone can hope</b></span>
  <span id="freeText14397243843169563569" style="display:none"><b>It all goes like that: </b> Q: Oh, fuck. Double thousand triple fuckity fuck. (c) <br /><br />The 2nd book is even better than the 1st one, imho. The author is going to be very careful so that the3d one doesn't repeat Harris' flop with his 3d vol of Hannibal Lecter.     <a title="Theresa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38029020-theresa"><img alt="Theresa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514840229p2/38029020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1546351254?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Theresa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Theresa" href="/user/show/38029020-theresa">Theresa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781476785622" href="/book/show/23492629-hidden-bodies">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38029020-theresa?shelf=mental-illness">mental-illness</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1546351254" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15972827793322584764">UPDATE: I had originally given "Hidden Bodies" 2 stars when I read it in July. Now that I've had time to fully digest it, I think I was actually too generous with my 2 star rating, a 1 star rating is much more appropriate. <br/><br/>What the hell did I just read?!?! I'll be honest, I felt like "You" was perfect the way it ended. "You" is one of my favorite novels I've read this year. It's unique, (second person narrative) sexy, intriguing, and beautifully written. So by the time, the sequel, "Hidden Bodie</span>
  <span id="freeText15972827793322584764" style="display:none">UPDATE: I had originally given "Hidden Bodies" 2 stars when I read it in July. Now that I've had time to fully digest it, I think I was actually too generous with my 2 star rating, a 1 star rating is much more appropriate. <br /><br />What the hell did I just read?!?! I'll be honest, I felt like "You" was perfect the way it ended. "You" is one of my favorite novels I've read this year. It's unique, (second person narrative) sexy, intriguing, and beautifully written. So by the time, the sequel, "Hidden Bodies" was released in February, I was reluctant to read it. All my close friends seemed to enjoy it, so I decided to keep an open-mind and give it a chance. You know, sometimes I really need to listen to that little voice in my head saying, "No, don't read it, it won't be as good as the original!" Well, I've learned my lesson. Intuition is good, peer-pressure is bad!<br /><br />"Hidden Bodies" is a 400+ train wreck. Joe is a pretentious know-it-all this time around. All his creepy but likeable charm is gone. I didn't root for him like I did in "You". I didn't really care about his obsessive need for revenge this time around. The whole Amy Adam storyline was completely pointless. If Joe is so smart like he claims to be, why couldn't he tell Amy was not a nice person? You want to know why? Because Joe sees what he wants to see. He thinks with his dick. Just being honest. Speaking of private parts, there was WAY TOO MUCH VULGARITY in this book! I swear it's all about sex, sex, and more sex. I'm not a prude but I got sick of hearing about Joe's sexual appetite every other page. Less is more, Caroline Kepnes. Now there were graphic sex scenes in "You" but the sexual tension was much more appealing in that book. Joe "chased" Beck. Joe doesn't have to "chase" anybody in "Hidden Bodies" because EVERY woman wants him. So unrealistic. How "hot" could this lonely, angry, depressed, pathetic little nerd be? Just saying. <br /><br />The pacing of the plot is slow-moving. Halfway though, we are introduced to Love and Forty (yes, those are names, their parents are big tennis fans). Joe begins a sexual relationship with Love VERY quickly. He loves to be in Love. His words, not mine. Gross. And Joe becomes friends with the irresponsible and drug-addicted, Forty. Truthfully, this when I lost interest in the story. Basically, a bunch of silly crap unravels and Joe does what he does best...gets revenge. We meet other characters like Henderson and Delilah, and Love and Forty's idiot parents but really, who cares? Long story short, NOTHING HAPPENS IN THIS BOOK! Well, nothing of value anyway. The ending is dumb and predictable and I'm 95% sure there will be a third book, but I won't waste my time and money reading it. This book suuuuuuucks! <br /><br />Worst line:<br /><br />"She kisses me as my cock delves into her and we are perfect together and I am better for knowing her and I'm still convinced that there's a special department in heaven where they build vaginas and if you're lucky like I am, one day you happen upon the one that was build for you." <br /><br />Eww! I'm going to pretend this travesty of a novel NEVER happened.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15972827793322584764" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15139778845161915889"><br/><b>4.5 Stars</b><br/><br/> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443706706i/16398608.jpg' width='400' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>I don't think I've ever loved a murderer as much I as love Joe Goldberg. I'm not sure if I should admit to that, but I don't care, he is just so damn entertaining. Caroline Kepnes has created one of the most fascinating characters I've ever had the pleasure to read. I'm not trying to turn into a gushing fangirl, but in all honestly I find her storytelling, her characters, and her writing simply brilliant. <i>Hidden Bodies</i> is quirky and addicting, with an element of underlying dark humor,</span>
  <span id="freeText15139778845161915889" style="display:none"><br><b>4.5 Stars</b><br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443706706i/16398608.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I don't think I've ever loved a murderer as much I as love Joe Goldberg. After things with Beck crashed and burned, he finds Amy, she is everything Beck wasn't, maybe he got it right this time? Or maybe not, when she robs him and takes off to Hollywood, Joe decides he has to find her, they were happy and he loved her, why would she do this??? <br><br><i>
  <b>She knew I was fucked up and alone. She knew I wanted a blowjob and a girlfriend and she knew I wanted these things so badly that I would let her watch Cocktail fifty times a fucking week in my bed, that I would give her a fucking key. I did that and I can't undo it. But I can find her. I can eliminate her.</b>
</i><br><br>Arriving in California Joe finds himself doing things he was adamantly against, he joins Facebook, makes friends, all part of his plan to find and punish Amy, but something unexpected happens, he meets Love.<br><br><i>
  <b>Amy and I had sex and heat. Beck dangled a carrot and I bit. But Love and I grow the carrots, and peel them, and eat them together.</b>
</i><br><br><i>Hidden Bodies</i> introduces a whole new cast of characters, and Joe's body count continues to climb. With a few unexpected twist and turns and the dreaded <i>mugofurine</i> plaguing his mind, Joe's life is constantly changing, but he may find more than revenge in LA, he may finally find love. <br><br><br><i>*ARC provided via Netgalley in exchange for an honest review* </i></span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1321939849" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1321939849" />
    <a title="Edward Lorn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn"><img alt="Edward Lorn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492199506p2/8850418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1321939849?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edward Lorn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edward Lorn" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn">Edward Lorn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/23492288-hidden-bodies">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1321939849" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5455047612214295217"><b>Just got an email from Amazon that my hardcover has shipped! Can I get a "FUCK YEAH!" Also, I'm bumping this review to remind everyone that this comes out in two days, February 23. Buy it. Buy one to read and one to collect. Buy your friend a copy. Buy your pet chinchilla Bernie a copy! </b><br/><br/><b>WINNER: BEST BOOK OF 2015!</b><br/><br/>From the jump, we will get rid of my one and only complaint. I prefer the original title of this book. According to GoodReads, <i>Hidden Bodies</i> was originally entitled <i>Love</i>. I can only imag</span>
  <span id="freeText5455047612214295217" style="display:none"><b>Just got an email from Amazon that my hardcover has shipped! Can I get a "FUCK YEAH!" Also, I'm bumping this review to remind everyone that this comes out in two days, February 23. Buy it. Buy one to read and one to collect. Buy your friend a copy. Buy your pet chinchilla Bernie a copy! </b><br /><br /><b>WINNER: BEST BOOK OF 2015!</b><br /><br />From the jump, we will get rid of my one and only complaint. I prefer the original title of this book. According to GoodReads, <i>Hidden Bodies</i> was originally entitled <i>Love</i>. I can only imagine the publishers and/or author decided to change it because there are roughly a quadrillion books with "Love" in their titles. This is unfortunate because <i>Love</i> is the perfect title for this novel. It covers the theme and the plot and the subtext. Everything in this book is about love. No worries, though, as this book is far removed from sappy. <br /><br /><i>Hidden Bodies</i> is one of those rare books that surpasses the pop culture material it references. You'll see nods to <i>Mr Mercedes</i> and <i>Less Than Zero</i>, and while the majority of this book happens in the same state as Bret Easton Ellis's debut novel, Caroline Kepnes's book resides in a world all its own. <br /><br /><i>Hidden Bodies</i> also claims a rare spot in literature by being a sequel that does not suck. It is, in my opinion, as good as its predecessor. <i>Hidden Bodies</i> is a different animal. It has different scenery. A different story to tell. Different characters. Even a different style of prose.<br /><br />Kepnes's debut effort, <i>You</i>, was written in second-person present tense; our narrator Joe Goldberg speaks directly to the woman currently holding his interest, as if she's always there to listen. It was a fresh experience. It worked to cement the tone of the work. Besides, there will never be another <i>You</i> like Guinevere Beck. <i>Hidden Bodies</i> is written in first-person present. This switch is needed because we do not follow one obsession throughout the novel. For a goodly amount of time, the reader hasn't a clue who Joe is going to latch onto next, or if he'll get the revenge he feels he deserves. All that is only a small part of the magic going on inside <i>Hidden Bodies</i>.<br /><br />Kepnes has a talent for sleight of hand. "Hey, you, look over here while I do this other thing behind your back." Twice in the same novel, I forgot what kind of person our narrator is. I'd be riding along on cruise control, enjoying how Kepnes turned a phrase, or I'd be snickering at some reference that is certainly only there for fanservice, and then Joe would remind me how truly unstable he is. This was as effective as a deer jumping in front of my car in the middle of city traffic. The first bathroom scene is one of the best since <i>Psycho</i> (I do not say that lightly), and it is made all that more effective by being in the psycho's head. The second bathroom scene had my heart playing "Wipeout" on my ribs. That was intense. I've not read a scene that nerve shattering in a long time. <br /><br />Finally, I must give credit to the author for caring about every single character she brought on stage, right down to Harvey. Yeah, I noticed. I actually shed a tear or two after finding out how he ends up. This was a small character, only referenced a handful of times, and Kepnes treated him with compassion and allowed him his own ending, his own complete albeit short story. Other authors would have moved on and forgotten about little ol' Harvey. This is what sets Kepnes apart from many novelists working today. You can tell she loves her cast, from the small roles to the horribly irredeemable ones. Moreover, this woman's writing is simply damn fun to read. <br /><br />I believe I have a new favorite novelist, friends and neighbors. <br /><br />In summation: Caroline Kepnes has her finger on the pulse of Today. She's counting the beats and taking notes. Because of this, she knows how to make our hearts race, how to steal them, and how to break them. Yes, <i>You</i> and <i>Hidden Bodies</i> are about a terrible human being, but it is in his mental illness that we all find the comfort of familiarity, because, as Robert Bloch once wrote, “I think perhaps all of us go a little crazy at times.” Highest possible recommendation. <br /><br /><b>Final Judgment: I feel bad for the rest of the books I have to read this year.</b><br /><br /><br /><i>(Thanks to Atria Publishing, NetGalley, and the author for allowing me to read an advance review copy of this novel. I almost wish you hadn't though, because I have no idea what to read next.) </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="5455047612214295217" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2210899251" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2210899251" />
    <a title="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68538597-booksofradiance"><img alt="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513125058p2/68538597.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2210899251?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" class="user" itemprop="url" name="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" href="/user/show/68538597-booksofradiance">❄️BooksofRadiance❄️</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781476785622" href="/book/show/23492629-hidden-bodies">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68538597-booksofradiance?shelf=crime-mystery-thriller">crime-mystery-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2210899251" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11314442758246291343">Nop. I think Joe deserves better than 3.75 stars (original rating). So I’m upping it to 4. <br/><br/>Right so, after the awesomeness of YOU, to say I was giddy with excitement to read Hidden Bodies would be a gross understatement. And, well... what I expected to get and what I got were two different things.<br/><br/>It’s nearly half a year since the concluding events of YOU and Joe’s got a new woman in his life, Amy Adam. He is completely smitten with her as she’s everything Beck (the girl who stole his heart in bo</span>
  <span id="freeText11314442758246291343" style="display:none">Nop. I think Joe deserves better than 3.75 stars (original rating). So I’m upping it to 4. <br /><br />Right so, after the awesomeness of YOU, to say I was giddy with excitement to read Hidden Bodies would be a gross understatement. And, well... what I expected to get and what I got were two different things.<br /><br />It’s nearly half a year since the concluding events of YOU and Joe’s got a new woman in his life, Amy Adam. He is completely smitten with her as she’s everything Beck (the girl who stole his heart in book #1) isn’t, and the pair enjoys a wild romance after Amy goes to work for Joe at Mooney Books. However, she too isn't all that she's cracked up to be as she steals rare first edition books from the store worth thousands of dollars and flees to Los Angeles without him knowing. <br />One might obviously say he has a type… <br />Joe’s angry AND impressed that someone could best him-ever the narcissist-; and despite his dislike of all things LA, he follows—or more accurately stalks—Amy to the West Coast, where he's soon immersed, much to his dismay, in the uninspired and pretentious lifestyle of Hollywood wannabes. <br /><br /><i>"Making it in Hollywood is the most disgusting phrase in the English language. It's more disturbing than prolific serial killer and rare uncurable decease."</i><br /><br />Now, onto what I liked and didn’t:<br /><b>what I loved:</b><br />Joe, Joe and… Joe in all his glories.<br /><br /><b>what I didn’t:</b><br />everything else.<br /><br />Joe didn't do much socialising with anyone outside of his beloved Beck, in YOU—which couldn't have been more perfect. I mean, call me greedy but I wanted him all to myself without the interruption of annoying side characters—, so, some might call the change in Hidden Bodies enlightening or… interesting, to see him interact with others for a change. I call it redundant and the rest of the cast - a hindrance. And FUCKING ANNOYING.<br /><br />Similarly to YOU, the characters were not particularly likeable nor relatable and I hated them all. There was not a single redeemable character—apart from… you guessed it—. I found them to be so painfully one-dimensional and lacking in depth, to say the least.<br /><br />I also found the plot underwhelming as it didn't have the same urgency and edge to it like YOU did. And though I liked that the ending was somewhat ambiguous with Joe's future undecided, I didn't like the execution one bit. So, why you ask, then did I give this 4 stars? because Joes is That. Dang. Good! He was the only thing that gave this book its worth. <br /><br />I've described him the best I could in my review of YOU but here’s a little more here:<br />He is still the same crazy and unhinged, batshit psychopath that we remember and this time around, I felt like I got a lot more out of him and his screwed up, demented principles.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“This, this is why you have to kill people. If you don’t, they don’t learn anything.”</i>
</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>"I cuffed his arms with cable ties. I know it's demeaning, I miss my cage where I didn't have to be reduced to this kind of thing."</i>
</b><br /><br />He’s scathing and charismatic as ever and his aura of charm and sophistication is still intact. His narrative voice is so blunt and uncensored, and he holds nothing back. He will stop at nothing to get what he wants and offing the people he comes across, be it of pure dislike or because they get in his way really doesn’t require a second thought. However, contrary to how he's described, he's neither bloodthirsty nor cold, far from it. It's simply a matter of - his way or no way. Or more accurately, his way or... death. He is also both self-aware and terribly deluded.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>“In the past, I had a tendency to be intense; you might even call it obsessive,”</b>
</i><br /><br /><i>
  <b>“Beck was such a mess that in order to take care of her, I had to follow her home and hack into her email and worry about her Facebook and her Twitter and her nonstop texting, all the contradictions, the lies.”</b>
</i><br /><br /><b>
  <i>"I’ve never harmed an animal. I can’t imagine being that sort of monster."</i>
</b> <br />I mean, the irony alone...😂<br /><br />In short, he’s a gem, guys!<br /><br />Now, before we wrap up, let’s go back to the ending, shall we? The way the plot was going, I didn't know what to expect but suffice it to say I <b>did not expect THAT. </b> Don't get me wrong, I was pleased with the fairly vague ending, however, just like with YOU, it felt incredibly rushed and not well thought out. It was as mashed-up as the plot was. <br /><br /><b>Trigger warning:</b> This novel contains scenes of explicit acts of physical violence, detailed descriptions of sexual acts and some substance abuse, particularly in terms of drug use. If these sound troubling to read, I highly advise steering clear of this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11314442758246291343" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13157087740985256502">You all will be happy to know that I have enjoyed Hidden Bodies significantly more that <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20821614.You__You___1_' title='You (You, #1) by Caroline Kepnes' rel='nofollow noopener'>You</a>! I'm still not sure why I had a hard time taking a liking to her first book. Maybe because I felt so much of the beginning was setting up the story, whereas in this book the story is full blown and we are thrown back in the middle of it. I actually liked Joe more in this book than the last one; I also felt the author's writing was stronger this go around. Definitely a believer now and am anticipating anot</span>
  <span id="freeText13157087740985256502" style="display:none">You all will be happy to know that I have enjoyed Hidden Bodies significantly more that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20821614.You__You___1_" title="You (You, #1) by Caroline Kepnes" rel="nofollow noopener">You</a>! I'm still not sure why I had a hard time taking a liking to her first book. Maybe because I felt so much of the beginning was setting up the story, whereas in this book the story is full blown and we are thrown back in the middle of it. I actually liked Joe more in this book than the last one; I also felt the author's writing was stronger this go around. Definitely a believer now and am anticipating another book from her in the future!<br /><br />Thank you so much Netgalley for this copy in exchange for an honest and fair review.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1438896564" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16330023870425798811">“HIDDEN BODIES” by Caroline Kepnes, is the follow-up to her debut novel, “YOU”, the continuation of an evil serial killer …Joe Goldberg.<br/><br/>I have to say that I enjoyed this book so much better than book 1. I had a hard time reading YOU, book 1, a dark psychological thriller that is not a book for everyone. "You" is not the book for you if you are easily offended by coarse language or scenes of a sexual nature. <br/><br/>In "YOU", we see Joe's involvement with Beck and later ended with Amy. But Amy is nothing</span>
  <span id="freeText16330023870425798811" style="display:none">“HIDDEN BODIES” by Caroline Kepnes, is the follow-up to her debut novel, “YOU”, the continuation of an evil serial killer …Joe Goldberg.<br /><br />I have to say that I enjoyed this book so much better than book 1. I had a hard time reading YOU, book 1, a dark psychological thriller that is not a book for everyone. "You" is not the book for you if you are easily offended by coarse language or scenes of a sexual nature. <br /><br />In "YOU", we see Joe's involvement with Beck and later ended with Amy. But Amy is nothing like Beck. Amy doesn’t use social media which means he can't keep tabs on her like he could with Beck.<br /><br />“I buy violets for Amy. Not roses. Roses are for people who did something wrong. I have done everything right this time around. I’m a good boyfriend. I chose well.”<br /><br />But one day Amy steals from him and disappears. And Joe is right on her tail! He leaves New York and moves to Hollywood to track her down. He wants ...revenge!<br /><br />Here in Hollywood, Joe works in a bookstore, and keeps a low profile. He is still haunted by his past.<br /><br />But would his past secrets remain buried? What if she finds out?<br /><br />I stood through it to see where the sequel, "Hidden Bodies" would take Joe. Maybe we had to see the bad to appreciate the change in the character. When I first started reading this book, I found it so different…but in a good way! Joe wants to change his life for the better, so he puts his past behind him, his buried victims, and moves to Los Angeles to start a new life. He is looking for a new start and true LOVE.<br /><br />There is still plenty of foul language and explicit scenes that may disturb some readers in this book, but I didn't actually find this sequel quite as dark as the first book, Joe seemed more human in this book, and more likeable...if you can like a serial killer!<br /><br />Many thanks to the publisher for providing me with an ARC via NetGalley.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16330023870425798811" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1228297310" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3924486094164902215">Did this book really take me nine days to read?! That alone tells the whole story. I put this on the hold the second I heard about it. I expected it to be published in September of last year. Waiting until February was torturous, though not, as it turns out, as torturous as trying to get through this bizarre sequel. I understand that the author was poking fun at LA but this was too long, too over-the-top, and too unbelievable for me. Joe, what happened to YOU?! 2 stars.<br/></span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

    <a title="Matthew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew"><img alt="Matthew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464987365p2/16254355.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2267146808?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew">Matthew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781442385672" href="/book/show/24999107-hidden-bodies">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2267146808" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10603559232839609217">A 2-star Californian soap opera. A sequel to You? Ehhh . . . sort of. I probably would have liked it more as a stand-alone with no tie ins to You. Our main character and a few plot points carry over, but it pales in comparison. It felt like the author had a book idea and tried her best to tie it in as a sequel.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1565184183ra/27951914.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I mention Californian soap opera, and so does Joe. He equates the world he is living in to the SNL skit The Californians – after which I could not get that out of my mind. Thus, all the fu</span>
  <span id="freeText10603559232839609217" style="display:none">A 2-star Californian soap opera. A sequel to You? Ehhh . . . sort of. I probably would have liked it more as a stand-alone with no tie ins to You. Our main character and a few plot points carry over, but it pales in comparison. It felt like the author had a book idea and tried her best to tie it in as a sequel.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1565184183ra/27951914.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I mention Californian soap opera, and so does Joe. He equates the world he is living in to the SNL skit The Californians – after which I could not get that out of my mind. Thus, all the fun gifs you are seeing throughout my review. And, he was right! This book felt just like that skit – or an episode of 90210 with a little murder included.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1565184183ra/27951912.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Whereas the first book was unique, shocking, and thrilling - this book was kind of just silly. Joe went from being a creep you end up cheering for to a totally irrational buffoon. The scenarios he gets involved with are so far fetched and laughable. I can honestly say it almost feels like someone wrote a parody of You.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1565184183ra/27951913.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The main character in this book really is the mug of piss from the first book. At least, Joe talks about the mug of piss at least once every few pages. I have reached my quota of the phrase “mug of piss” for life!<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="10603559232839609217" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
